Much of his childhood  was made unhappy by unsuccessful attempts to cure a  lame foot, of which he remained painful1y conscious.  He inherited the title in 1798 and went to live in the  family home, Newstead Abbey, Nottinghamshire.  At Harrow and Trinity College, Cambridge, he not  only read eagerly but took pride in overcoming his  lameness by boxing, playing cricket and becoming  a powerful swimmer. In 1807 he published Hours  of Idleness, which was savagely criticised in the  Edinburgh Review. He withdrew it and replied  with the satire English Bards and Scotch Reviewers.
